801 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Hurd v. Buffalo


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


41 A.D.2d 402; 343 N.Y.S.2d 950; 1973 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 4430



May 18, 1973 



DISPOSITION: Judgment unanimously reversed on the law with costs and judgment declared in favor of plaintiffs in accordance with opinion by Moule, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizen appealed from an order of the Supreme Court (New York), which entered judgment for defendant city in the citizen's action challenging the city's levy of real property tax of $ 73,923,246, including $ 23,327,290 for pension and retirement payments, upon the taxable real estate in the city. The trial court declared that N.Y. Local Fin. Law § 11-42(a) was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The citizen contended that the tax imposed exceeded the proper tax levies by $ 17,707,313 because of the pension and retirement payments. The city argued that the benefits of the payments had useful periods beyond one year. The trial court had upheld N.Y. Local Fin. Law § 11-42(a). The court reversed, finding that § 11-42(a) was without a rational basis and was arbitrary. The cases relied on by the city were one-time fundings of obligations, not ongoing payments. All of the city's expenditures could be considered to have a usefulness outliving the fiscal year when they were made, which would render the constitutional restriction meaningless. The citizens of the state of New York, in establishing a constitutional tax limit of two percent for operating expenses, presumably decided that it was the maximum tax which could be levied on real property without becoming oppressive, and it could not be circumvented by legislation. The court did not order repayment, finding that the city administration had relied upon the statute in preparing its budget and to mandate repayment of amounts illegally collected in the past would place an impossible burden upon it.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the city upholding the tax levy and entered a judgment in favor of the citizen.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- pensions -- constitutional limitation -- trial court erred in not declaring unconstitutional section of Local Finance Law insofar as it excepts taxes on real property for city pension and retirement liabilities from tax total constitutionally required to be within percentage limit of formulated valuation of city's taxable real estate -- taxes already illegally collected need not be returned.

1. The trial court erred in not declaring unconstitutional as arbitrary and without rational basis paragraph 42-a of subdivision a of section 11.00 of the Local Finance Law insofar as it excepts the City of Buffalo's future annual requirement for pension and retirement liabilities from those taxes the total of which must not exceed the real property tax limit, as defined in section 10 of article VIII of the New York Constitution,  [***2] of 2% of the average full valuation of the city's taxable real estate. Subdivision (b) of section 11 of article VIII excepts those taxes, from such limit, levied for the payment of direct budgetary appropriations for purposes which have a period of probable usefulness determined by law. Paragraph 42-a, by declaratory description, categorizes the pension and retirement liabilities so as to comply with the constitutional exception; if such statute were valid, most periodic city expenditures could be similarly excepted and the constitutional limitation rendered meaningless.

2. The city need not repay the tax moneys illegally collected and already spent in reliance upon the statute; such mandate would place an impossible burden on the city and, as a doctrine, would inhibit implementation of statutes until tested by the courts.

 

802 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Wright v. Town Bd. of Carlton


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


41 A.D.2d 290; 342 N.Y.S.2d 577; 1973 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 4731



April 13, 1973 



DISPOSITION: Judgment modified on the law and facts in accordance with opinion by Cardamone, J., and as so modified affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant electors sought review of the judgment of the Supreme Court (New York) which denied the electors' petition to rescind and annul the actions of respondent town board in creating a water district.


OVERVIEW: A referendum was held on the town board's proposal to create a water district that included the entire township. All qualified electors were permitted to vote, not just the owners of taxable real property. After the proposition was approved, some of the electors filed a petition to rescind and annul the actions of the town board. The trial court denied the petition. On appeal, the court modified the trial court's judgment, but otherwise affirmed it. First, the court held that N.Y. Town Law § 209-e(3), which limited the franchise to the owners of taxable real property, was unconstitutional, except upon a showing that nonowners of property were substantially less interested than property owners in the outcome of the referendum and that the exclusion of nonproperty owners was necessary to promote a compelling state interest. Those challenging the referendum failed to make that showing. Next, the court held that the town board did not abuse its legislative power and discretion in its creation of the water district's boundary lines. The court modified the judgment only insofar as the trial court determined that the electors' challenge to the benefit method of assessment was premature.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment dismissing the electors' petition to rescind and annul the actions of the town board in creating a water district, except that the judgment was modified insofar as the trial court determined that the electors' challenge to the benefit method of assessment was premature.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- water district -- not only "owners of taxable real property" ( Town Law, § 209-e, subd. 3), but all qualified residents, are constitutionally entitled to vote on creation of proposed water district -- Town Board properly determined that water district's boundaries should be same as town's, and that costs of district should be assessed on properties according to benefits received -- actual assessment amounts have not yet been determined and hence cannot be reviewed.

1. Despite the provision in the Town Law ( § 209-e, subd. 3) that the voters on a proposition for the creation of a water district shall be "the owners of taxable real property situate in the proposed district", qualified resident electors who do not own real property are constitutionally [***2] entitled to vote too. They are not substantially less interested, and there is no compelling State interest or reason for excluding them.

2. After a public hearing, the Town Board properly determined that all property within the town would be benefited by the creation of a water district and that therefore the district's boundaries should be the same as the town's boundaries. Such determination was legislative and discretionary and the court will not reverse it.

3. The Town Board further properly determined that the costs of the district should be assessed, not according to the assessed valuations of real properties, but according to the benefits received by the different real properties ( Town Law, § 209-q, subd. 6, pars. [c], [e]).

4. However, the Town Board has not levied or determined any assessment amounts yet, and it is not bound by the schedule of assessments suggested in the report of its consulting engineers; so any attack on assessment amounts is, as yet, premature (cf. Town Law, §§ 236, 237, 239; § 209-q, subd. 6, par. [e]).

 

803 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Yax v. Evans


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


41 A.D.2d 232; 342 N.Y.S.2d 453; 1973 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 4726



April 13, 1973 



DISPOSITION: Order unanimously affirmed with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant town sought review of an order of the Supreme Court of Erie County (New York), which granted respondent property owner's motion for summary judgment in the property owner's action challenging a local law as violative of the state constitution and N.Y. Town Law § 130(16).


OVERVIEW: The town's building inspector determined that two residential buildings of the property owner were unfit, unsafe, and a menace to public health, welfare, and safety. Pursuant to the provisions of local law, he notified the property owner by certified mail that the structures had to be repaired, removed, or demolished. The inspector posted a similar notice on the structures. The mailed notice came back through the mail, and the inspector handed a copy to the property owner's husband when he came to the inspector's office to discuss the matter. At the meeting, the inspector told the husband that he had six months to make repairs. Without further notice or contact, the buildings were demolished. The property owner asserted that she had made improvements to the premises after the service of the notice and had brought the buildings into compliance. The court upheld the judgment granted to the property owner, finding that the local law was unconstitutional. The law was inconsistent with N.Y. Town Law § 130(16) because it failed to require an application for an order granting permission to demolish the structures. Therefore, the local law was invalid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting the property owner's motion for summary judgment.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- removal of buildings -- Local Law No. 1 of Town of Evans does not meet standards of Town Law ( § 130, subd. 16) set for repair or removal of buildings and is invalid.

The New York State Constitution (art. IX, § 2, subd. [c], subpar. [ii], cl. [10]) allows local governments to adopt laws pertaining to the protection, order, conduct, safety, health and well-being of persons or property therein "not inconsistent with the provisions of * * * any general law". The Municipal Home Rule Law ( § 10, subd. 1, par. [ii], subpar. a, cl. [11]) gives local governments the same power. The Town Law ( § 130, subd. 16) lays out specific provisions for legislation for the repair or removal of buildings. Local Law No. 1 of the Town of Evans does not meet the standards of the Town Law ( § 130, subd. 16). The most apparent defects are: defective notice requirements; failure to require the inspector, when designating an unfit building, to [***2] make a report; failure to provide for a survey; failure to provide for a motion at Special Term prior to the destruction of buildings and the provision that assessments be made against the owner or occupant of the premises rather than against the land. Local Law No. 1 is invalid.

 

804 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Bellamy v. Judges & Justices Authorized to Sit in New York City Criminal Court


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


41 A.D.2d 196; 342 N.Y.S.2d 137; 1973 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 4807



April 3, 1973 



DISPOSITION: Judgment unanimously granted in favor of defendants declaring that the bail system attacked by plaintiffs is constitutional, and that there is no proper basis for a class action; and, insofar as relief is sought under article 78 of the CPLR, the application [***2] is denied and the petition dismissed, without costs and without disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs petitioned under a N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78 proceeding for a declaratory judgment that New York State's present bail system violated the rights guaranteed them by the U.S. Constitution and the laws of New York State.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, on behalf of themselves as criminal defendants and as a class action, sought a declaratory judgment that the bail system for those facing criminal charges in New York County violated the equal protection and due process clauses of the U.S. Constitution, as well as the Eighth Amendment and federal constitutional prohibitions against excessive bail. Specifically, plaintiffs argued that the bail system was unfair because it denied poor people their freedom pending a trial and that the denial of bail inevitably led to conviction. The court found that there was no proper basis for a class action because there were individual determinations made in every bail application and denied the relief requested. The court further found that it was not because bail was required that a criminal defendant was later convicted, but because he was likely to be convicted that bail was required. The court granted judgment declaring that the bail system was constitutional, that there was no basis for a class action, and dismissed the petition seeking to prohibit the present system.


OUTCOME: Judgment was granted declaring New York's bail system constitutional because bail system had a rational relationship to and was adjusted to a criminal defendant's circumstances, and there were procedures for judicial review of bail determinations.


HEADNOTES

Bail -- constitutional law -- present bail system is constitutional -- class action dismissed.

1. The present bail system ( CPL art. 500 et seq.), as correctly applied, does not violate constitutional principles (cf. U. S. Const., 8th and 14th Amdts.; N. Y. Const., art. I, § 5).

2. Since every bail determination is individual, and furthermore can be judicially reviewed ( CPL 460.50; CPLR 7002), there is no basis for a class action or class proceeding ( CPLR 1005, subd. [a]).

 

805 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Brighenti v. Judges of New York Supreme Court


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


41 A.D.2d 209; 342 N.Y.S.2d 123; 1973 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 4811



April 2, 1973 



DISPOSITION: Application granted, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner defendants sought to prohibit respondents, justices and a district attorney, from proceeding further with the prosecution of a kidnapping indictment pending against defendants. Defendants asserted that a trial under the kidnapping indictment would have placed them in double jeopardy in violation of their rights under U.S. Const. Amend. V and N. Y. Const. art. I, § 6.


OVERVIEW: Defendants had been indicted and pleaded guilty under the Federal Bank Robbery Statute, 18 U.S.C.S. § 2113. The court granted defendants' petition. The court held as follows: 1) count three of the federal indictment, to which defendants pleaded guilty, alleged the underlying facts constituting the robbery and, additionally, set forth facts showing forcible accompaniment without consent, in violation of § 2113(e); 2) the crimes charged in counts one and three of the federal indictment were separate and distinct; 3) while § 2113(e) did not explicitly define the crime therein as kidnapping, it nonetheless spelled out kidnapping within the purview of the federal bank robbery statute; and 4) a final judgment having been rendered on the federal charge, defendants had been twice placed in jeopardy by the pending county kidnapping indictment, in violation of their constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendants' application to prohibit further prosecution of the kidnapping charge.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- former jeopardy -- crime of forcing bank manager to accompany petitioners as hostage in course of robbing national bank, to which crime under Federal law petitioners pleaded guilty, is same crime, kidnapping, of which petitioners are accused in State indictment; prosecution under State indictment is prohibited since it would subject petitioners to second prosecution for same crime.

Petitioners pleaded guilty to count three of a four-count Federal indictment, arising from robbery of a national bank and taking the manager as hostage, charging petitioners with forcible accompaniment without consent in violation of subdivision (e) of section 2113 of title 18 of the United States Code. The other counts were dismissed. Subdivision (e) of the Federal statute provides that "Whoever, in committing any offense defined in this section * * * forces any person to accompany him without the consent of such person, shall be imprisoned". While such subdivision [***2] does not explicitly define the crime therein as kidnapping, it nonetheless spells out kidnapping within the purview of the Federal bank robbery statute. Prosecution under an indictment against petitioners handed down by the Richmond County Grand Jury charging kidnapping in the first and second degrees is prohibited. The Federal indictment included the charge of kidnapping which is the gravamen of the State indictment. The charges are essentially the same. The Richmond County indictment places petitioners twice in jeopardy for the same crime.

 

806 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Blumberg v. Yonkers


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


41 A.D.2d 300; 341 N.Y.S.2d 977; 1973 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 4830



March 26, 1973 



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Supreme Court, Westchester County, entered September 7, 1972, affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners challenged the judgment of the Supreme Court, Westchester County (New York), which dismissed their complaint against defendant city in their action to enjoin the use of real property for the purpose of erecting a supermarket.


OVERVIEW: The property owner's parcel adjoined the lot on which the construction of a supermarket was proposed. The property owners challenged the enactment of a city ordinance changing the zoning for the area on the ground that it was simply a reenactment of an ordinance already declared invalid. The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, holding that the ordinance was valid. The court found that because the previous ordinance was held invalid, it did not prevent a subsequent rezoning if it was based on a comprehensive plan rather than spot zoning. A change in zoning would be upheld if it did not conflict with the community's basic scheme of land use. The ordinance at issue was an attempt to zone the entire city. Moreover, the change in zoning by permitting the construction of a supermarket was not in conflict with the city's comprehensive plan. The court rejected the property owner's argument that they had no notice of the public hearings concerning the reenactment, finding that although N.Y. Gen. City Law § 83 did not require the city to publish the notice in the newspaper, the city published the notice of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court in favor of the city in the property owner's action to enjoin the construction of a supermarket on adjoining property.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- zoning -- enactment after sufficient notice of comprehensive, citywide zoning ordinance, rationally conceived with consideration of community's land use problems, which changed 13-lot area in City of Yonkers into district permitting supermarket and accessory parking use, which was in harmony with surrounding neighborhood, was proper.

In 1953, an ordinance of the City of Yonkers zoned 1 through 4 of 13 contiguous lots on Riverdale Avenue near the New York City line as "BA" commercial, changing the rest to A-1 residential. Attempts by successive [***2] owners to obtain city permission to build a supermarket on lots 1 through 4 plus a part of 5 and to use the remaining lots for accessory parking were either denied at the Zoning Board of Appeals or city Common Council levels or struck down in the courts, once under an article 78 proceeding establishing no right to a variance based upon a hardship self-imposed by knowingly purchasing the lots for a prohibited use, and again in a suit for a declaratory judgment determining that a 1962 ordinance specifying lots 5 through 13 for use only for accessory parking was spot zoning not adopted pursuant to a comprehensive plan. In 1970, the Yonkers Common Council re-enacted (G.O. No. 39-1970) a 1968 citywide, comprehensive zoning ordinance (G.O. No. 24-1968) which, among other changes, put all 13 lots into a "B" zone district permitting supermarket and accessory parking use. The re-enacted ordinance was properly upheld by the trial court as applied to these 13 lots because the over-all comprehensive plan was rationally created with forethought to the community's land use problems; the change was not antagonistic to the city's comprehensive zoning plan and was in harmony with the surrounding [***3] neighborhood; procedurally, the 1970 ordinance was enacted after sufficient notice, and any issue as to whether the ordinance is void because it adopts by reference penal provisions is not before the court as no attempt has been made to enforce such provisions, if any exist, and the contention was not raised at Special Term.

 

807 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Fermaglich v. Levine


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


41 A.D.2d 70; 341 N.Y.S.2d 394; 1973 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 5394



March 8, 1973 



DISPOSITION: Decision reversed, with costs, and matter remitted to the Unemployment Insurance Appeal Board for further proceedings not inconsistent herewith.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Claimant employee challenged a decision of the Unemployment Insurance Appeal Board (New York) that sustained respondent commissioner's determination that the employee was not entitled to benefits because he lost his job as a federal postal inspector through misconduct.


OVERVIEW: While still a probationary employee of the United States Post Office, the employee was terminated, and he filed a claim for unemployment benefits. On a wage and separation information form, the federal agency reported that the termination was the result of the employee's having been apprehended for theft of mail even though the indictment against him had been dismissed. As a result of this information, the commissioner denied the employee's request for benefits based on misconduct, and although a referee reversed that decision, it was affirmed by an appellate board. On appeal, the court reversed the decision of the appellate board, holding that the finding of misconduct was not supported by substantial evidence and that the federal agency had not found the employee guilty of mail fraud. The court found that no substantial evidence was submitted to show that the employee had stolen the mail; thus, the appellate board was not entitled to draw the factual conclusion from the literal language of the federal agency's report that the employee had actually stolen mail. The court concluded that the employee did not lose his employment because of misconduct.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate board's finding that the employee had been discharged for misconduct and was therefore not entitled to unemployment compensation benefits. The matter was remanded to the appellate board.


HEADNOTES

Unemployment insurance -- disqualification for benefits -- Federal employee, discharged before end of probationary term because apprehended for theft of mail, was improperly denied unemployment insurance benefits since there was no finding that employee was actually guilty of theft.

A Federal postal clerk, discharged before the end of his six-month probationary term "for being apprehended by a postal inspector for theft of mail" and because "Termination during probation 5/19/71 for being apprehended by the postal inspection service for the theft of mail on 5/3/71", was improperly denied unemployment insurance benefits by the Unemployment Insurance Appeal Board. The Federal agency's report states that claimant was apprehended for mail theft but does not by implication or otherwise constitute substantial evidence to infer that claimant had been found by the agency or his superiors to have actually stolen mail. The report establishes that [***2] claimant was charged with a theft of mail and for that reason, without coming to any conclusions as to guilt or innocence, the agency terminated the employment of the probationary employee. Being charged with an act which would constitute misconduct would not support a disqualification from benefits without a finding that the employee was guilty of misconduct, and here there is no evidence to support a finding of guilt of mail theft or of misconduct.

New York v. S & H Book Shop, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]

41 A.D.2d 637; 341 N.Y.S.2d 292; 1973 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 5025

809 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mobil Oil Corp.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


40 A.D.2d 369; 340 N.Y.S.2d 438; 1973 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 5177; 1973-1 Trade Cas. (CCH) P74,426



February 8, 1973 



DISPOSITION: Order, Supreme Court, New York County, entered on November 9, 1972, affirmed, without costs and without disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant corporation sought review of the order of the Supreme Court of New York, New York County, which denied its motion to quash plaintiff State's subpoena in an antitrust investigation.


OVERVIEW: The State, pursuant to the Donnelly Anti-Trust Act, N.Y. Gen. Bus. Law art. 22, filed an action against the corporation to enjoin and prevent violations of N.Y. Gen. Bus. Law § 340. As part of a continuing investigation, the State served a subpoena on the corporation to obtain data and documents relative to its practices concerning dealer aid. The corporation filed a motion to quash the subpoena. It argued that the State was utilizing the subpoena to circumvent the disclosure procedures in the civil practice law and rules and that enforcement of the subpoena would deprive it of its constitutional rights. The trial court denied the motion. The corporation appealed. The court affirmed the order because, pursuant to N.Y. Gen. Bus. Law § 343, the State's ability to conduct investigations and issue subpoenas was not terminated by the antitrust action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the corporation's motion to quash the State's subpoena.


HEADNOTES

Witnesses -- subpoena -- General Business Law ( § 343) pursuant to which Attorney-General served subpoena on defendant to obtain data and documents relative to its practices concerning dealer aid, not unconstitutional if construed to permit examination of one of defendants in circumvention of provisions of CPLR -- statute provides that power to issue subpoenas shall not terminate by reason of action or proceeding commenced -- Attorney-General specifically states that investigation is continuing.

After the commencement of an action by the Attorney-General pursuant to article 22 of the General Business Law (Donnelly Anti-Trust Act), to enjoin alleged violations of section 340 of that act, and as part of a continuing investigation, the Attorney-General served a subpoena on defendant pursuant to section 343 of the General Business [***2] Law to obtain data and documents relative to defendant's practices concerning dealer aid. That statute provides that the Attorney-General may conduct his investigations with authority to issue subpoenas which "shall not abate or terminate by reason of any action or proceeding brought by the attorney general under this article". The Attorney-General has specifically stated that the investigation is continuing. The section would not be unconstitutional if it were construed to permit an examination of a defendant in circumvention of the provisions of the CPLR.

 

810 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Sokolov v. Manorhaven


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


41 A.D.2d 570; 340 N.Y.S.2d 148; 1973 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 5239



January 29, 1973 



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed, on the law, without costs; the proceeding is hereby treated as a declaratory judgment action, with the petition deemed to be the complaint; and the relief therein requested is granted to the extent that the special assessment placed on petitioners' property is declared illegal and not in accordance with section 166 of the Village Law. The findings of fact below are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner landowners brought an action under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78 against respondents, a village and village officials (village), for a judgment declaring that a special assessment the village placed on the landowners for grading and paving of streets violated N.Y. Village Law § 166. The Supreme Court, Nassau County (New York), entered judgment for the village and dismissed the landowners' petition. The landowners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landowners had only 30 feet of frontage on one of five streets the village graded and paved. The village assessed the landowners for half the cost of paving all five streets. On appeal, the court, treating the landowners' action as one for declaratory judgment under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 103(c), reversed, entered a declaratory judgment for the landowners, and declared that the village's special assessment on the landowners was illegal and not in accordance with N.Y. Village Law § 166. The court held that § 166 prohibited the village from assessing the property owners for the expense of grading and paving any portion of any street not adjacent to the landowners' land. The court held that adjacent within the meaning of § 166 meant touching or contiguous, and that therefore the landowners could not be assessed for any portion of the five streets that was not touching their land. The court held that the village had no authority under N.Y. Village Law § 168 to levy the special assessment on the landowners.


OUTCOME: The court reversed, granted declaratory judgment for the landowners, and declared that the village's special assessment on the landowners was illegal and not in accordance with N.Y. Village Law § 166.

 

811 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Dobbs Ferry Medical Pavillion, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


40 A.D.2d 324; 340 N.Y.S.2d 108; 1973 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 5261



January 22, 1973 



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed, on the law and the facts, with one bill of costs jointly to the nonparty appellants against respondent, and complaint dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The appellant doctor sought review from an order of the Supreme Court at Special Term (New York), which enjoined the doctor and others from operating an abortion clinic without written approval of the Public Health Council of the State of New York.


OVERVIEW: The appellant doctor and others formed a partnership and leased a floor in a professional building. Three fourths of their practice was the performance of abortions. An official of the State Health concluded that the offices constituted a "hospital facility" under N.Y. Pub. Health Law art. 28, and requested the doctor to file an application for a license by the Public Health Counsel. The doctor refused, and the respondent state filed an action for injunction. The doctor argued that the hospital licensing statute, N.Y. Pub. Health Law §§ 2801, 2801-a, and related provisions of the Department of Health, N.Y. Comp. Codes R & Regs. tit. 10, § 700.2 were too vague. The trial court granted the injunction, and the doctor sought review. The court held that the trial court erred in determining that the doctor's practice was a "clinic" and therefore, a hospital facility under the statutory authority, because a clinic could also mean a group practice. The court held that N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 2801 and section 700.2 of the Sanitary Code, codified at N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 10, § 700.2 when considered together were vague, and therefore, unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed judgment in favor of the appellant doctor in an action filed by the respondent state to enjoin the doctor and others from performing abortions without a hospital license.


HEADNOTES

Abortion -- group medical practice -- group medical practice of abortions is not subject to licensing requirements for "hospital" or for "independent out-of-hospital health facility" (Public Health Law, art. 28; 10 NYCRR 700.2 [a] [6]); moreover, definitions in statute and regulation, as applied to this case, are unconstitutionally vague -- judgment which enjoins  [***2] "any other person with knowledge of this injunction" may be appealed from by such interested and adversely affected persons.

1. Three doctors have formed a partnership for the group practice of obstetrics, gynecology and general surgery. They share all income and expenses equally. They have many patients. Over three fourths of their patients come from other States, for abortions. Concededly these doctors are well qualified to perform abortions and their offices in Westchester County, N. Y., are adequately equipped for these procedures. They employ a business manager and pay him a fixed salary, and they pay their landlord a fixed rental. Neither their landlord nor their manager shares in their fees. Like all other doctors, they are subject to adequate supervision and control; moreover, the State Health Commissioner has power to inspect any building and to take appropriate action against any person who may be endangering health (Public Health Law, §§ 12-a, 16, 206, subd. 2). These doctors are in partnership for the group practice of a lawful specialty of medicine. They are not operating a "hospital" or an "independent out-of-hospital health facility" and they are not subject [***3] to the licensing conditions and requirements for such institutions (Public Health Law, art. 28, § 2801, subd. 1; 10 NYCRR 700.2 [a] [6]). Moreover, the definitions of "hospital" and of "independent out-of-hospital health facility" in the above-cited statute and regulation, when considered together, are unconstitutionally vague as written and as applied to this case.

2. A judgment which enjoins not only the named parties (the landlord and the business manager) but "any other person with knowledge of this injunction" may be appealed from by such interested and adversely affected persons (the three doctors in this group practice partnership).

 

812 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Hospital TVn Sys v. New York State Tax Comm'n


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


41 A.D.2d 576; 339 N.Y.S.2d 603; 1973 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 5363



January 17, 1973 



DISPOSITION: Order, insofar as appealed from, affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent New York State Tax Commission sought review of an order of the Supreme Court at Special Term in Albany County (New York), which, in denied the Commission motion to dismiss petitioner corporation's proceeding filed pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to the Commission making a determination and a demand for sales tax from the corporation, the corporation commenced an action under art. 78, which sought to annul the commission's determination on the ground that N.Y. Tax Law § 28 did not apply to the receipts of coin-operated television sets. The Commission contended that the corporation was required to exhaust its time-barred administrative remedy provided for in N.Y. Tax Law § 1138. Affirming the order of the lower court, the court held that where when a taxing authority's jurisdiction was challenged on the ground that the statute was unconstitutional or inapplicable, resort need not be had to the method of review prescribed in the taxing statute. The court found that the corporation contended that its activities were outside the scope of the sales tax and sought to prohibit the Commission from exceeding its jurisdiction by applying the sales tax law to the corporation's operation. Accordingly, the administrative remedy provided for in § 1138 was clearly inadequate for such purpose. The court concluded that the corporation could have properly maintained the N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78 proceeding.


OUTCOME: In so far as the order was appealed from, the court affirmed the lower court's order.

Jewish Reconstructionist Synagogue, Inc. v. Levitan


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]

815 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


In re Kimball


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


40 A.D.2d 252; 339 N.Y.S.2d 302; 1973 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 5378



January 8, 1973 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Application for admission to the Bar denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The applicant filed for admission to the state bar after the Committee on Character and Fitness reported that he possessed the requisite character and fitness for an attorney at law notwithstanding that admission of the applicant to being a homosexual and having engaged in homosexual acts.


OVERVIEW: The applicant, certified as having passed the bar examination, filed for admission to the bar. The court denied his application finding that he lacked the requisite character and fitness to be admitted to the bar. The Supreme Court of Florida disbarred the applicant after he was found guilty of behavior contrary to good morals and in violation of Florida law. The applicant had been accused of committing sodomy on a public beach. He had been arrested previously for the offense, had given a bail bond, and thereafter forfeited it. The applicant maintained his innocence of the charges. On independent view of the record, the court found that the evidence substantiated the findings of fact. The evidence raised issues of credibility and the referee in the Florida disbarment proceeding was entitled to decide those issues against the applicant. The court found that so long as N.Y. Penal Law § 130.38 was in effect, homosexuality, which, in its fulfillment, usually entailed commission of a statutorily proscribed act, was a factor which could militate against the eligibility of an applicant for admission to the bar who proposed to pursue his way of life in disregard of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court denied the application for admission to the bar after the applicant had been disbarred in Florida after he was found guilty of behavior contrary to good morals in violation of Florida law following his arrest for committing sodomy on a public beach at night.


HEADNOTES

Attorneys -- admission to Bar -- application for admission to Bar of this State by one who had been disbarred in Florida upon findings that he had committed sodomy denied -- disbarment in Florida does not foreclose exercise of judgment by New York courts -- New York not bound to give full faith and credit to Florida disbarment -- under New York law applicant would have been automatically disbarred -- initial admission may not be granted where he could not have been readmitted.

1. Matter of Peters (250 N. Y. 595) and the Judiciary Law ( § 90, subd. 5) do not foreclose the exercise of judgment by the New York courts in determining character and fitness of an applicant for admission to the Bar of this State, regardless of his disbarment in Florida. The fact of disbarment and the charges underlying the disbarment must be considered together with all the other circumstances, so that the total background of the applicant may be viewed to determine his character and fitness.

2. New York is not bound to give full faith and credit to the Florida judgment of disbarment.

3. Findings of fact in Florida that the applicant had committed [***2] sodomy were substantiated by the evidence, although the applicant continues to maintain his innocence.

4. The decision referred to by the applicant, who maintains that the statute under which he was arrested in 1955 was held unconstitutional by the Supreme Court of Florida, did not affect his conviction and subsequent disbarment, but, instead, ratified it.

5. Moreover, in 1955, at the time of the incident leading to the applicant's conviction, sodomy, even between consenting adults, was a felony in New York (former Penal Law, § 690). Accordingly, under our then laws, if the applicant had been an attorney in our State, he would have been automatically disbarred and he could not be readmitted except upon a reversal of the conviction or a pardon (Judiciary Law, § 90, subd. 5). If he could not have been readmitted, initial admission may not be granted.

6. The fact that at present the applicant's act would be considered a misdemeanor in Florida and would also be considered a class B misdemeanor under section 130.38 of our Penal Law does not affect the validity or propriety of the Florida disbarment.

7. The applicant did not produce any evidence in support of his contention before [***3] the committee that he was a victim of entrapment in the incident upon which his disbarment was based; nor did he make that contention at any time in the proceedings in Florida. There is nothing to indicate that the applicant was not granted a fair and full hearing in Florida.

8. There is no need to reach the question whether, as petitioner contends, the moral climate toward homosexuality has so changed since 1957 that his disbarment on that ground should not deter his admission to the Bar here.

9. The applicant lacks the requisite character and fitness to be admitted to the Bar in this State and his application should be denied.

 

816 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Lefrak Forest Hills Corp. v. Galvin


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


40 A.D.2d 211; 338 N.Y.S.2d 932; 1972 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2992



December 26, 1972 



DISPOSITION: Determination annulled, on the law, without costs, and Board of Standards and Appeals directed to issue an extension of the permits for one year beginning from the date of the order entered hereon.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner developers filed proceedings under N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 to annul determinations by respondent Board of Standards and Appeals of the City of New York (board), which denied applications by the developers for extensions of permits for the construction of apartment buildings that had been challenged by the intervenor individuals.


OVERVIEW: The developers were the last in a series of parties who were trying to construct a high rise apartment building over a railroad right of way in the face of vigorous opposition by the individuals. The board had granted numerous extensions over the course of several years, when it changed its opinion and denied the developers permit for further extensions. In a proceeding for extraordinary relief the court held that: (1) the operative zoning regulations had not restricted the transfer of permits or property, (2) formal acknowledgment of judicial concepts such as the res judicata doctrine was not necessary in the administrative circumstance under consideration, but due regard for principled decisions made in the past that concerned the same project was desirable, (3) the developers had acquired a vested right in the project under consideration by virtue of the combined force of prior determinations by the board and the expenditures and liabilities of the developers made in reliance on those determinations that could not be set aside.


OUTCOME: The court held that the determination of the board, which had denied an extension, should be annulled and the board was directed to issue an extension of the requested permits for one year from the date of the court's order.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- building permits -- after city Board of Standards and Appeals granted seven extensions of building permits for construction of large apartment buildings over railroad right of way over period of 10 years and after petitioners acquired ownership, city agreeing to alter last building permit to show petitioners' changes in plans, board denied eighth renewal; denial is annulled and respondent directed to issue permit -- petitioners did not need possessory interest -- in face of prior extensions and petitioners' expenditures and reliance on prior permits, board  [***2] improperly exercised discretion.

1. In 1961, the Long Island Railroad sold part of its right of way for the construction of apartment houses over the right of way, the railroad retaining a perpetual easement over the property for railroad purposes. A new zoning resolution became effective on December 15, 1961, which permitted apartment houses but at a lesser scale. The purchaser obtained building permits for construction of the apartment houses as originally contemplated. Work started on the project but had not been completed. Extensions of the permits were granted for two years. One-year additional extensions were granted until 1967, when the builder defaulted and a bank holding a mortgage became the owner at a foreclosure sale. The bank obtained four additional one-year extensions and in April, 1971 contracted to sell the property to petitioners. Petitioners changed the plans and the building permit was amended accordingly. On December 10, 1971 they applied for an additional year's extension which the Board of Standards and Appeals denied. Such denial is annulled and the applications should be granted.

2. The 1960 Zoning Resolution did not require a possessory interest [***3] and it did not prohibit the transfer of building permits or of the property.

3. The board granted a series of seven applications for extensions to build, the last four having been made by a bank which was seeking a builder with the means and ability to undertake a construction of considerable size. When the bank succeeded in finding a builder, the board reversed its prior rulings, all of which had been sustained by the courts, and determined that the development was not appropriate and that work on the foundations had not been substantially completed. The exercise of discretion by the board in denying the present extension cannot be disassociated from its exercise of discretion in granting past extensions. While the board could take into account the long delay in completing the construction, it could not ignore its own determinations to condone the delay and its own findings of substantial construction and appropriateness of the property for the relief granted. The exercise of discretion in refusing another extension is beyond justification in the face of petitioners' large expenditures and their contracting of liabilities, on the strength of the extensions, after they had purchased [***4] the property. Petitioners acquired a vested right to proceed under their permits in the light of the combined force of the prior determination of the board, upheld by the courts, the expenditures made in reliance on the permits prior to the time petitioners purchased the property, and the expenditures and the assumption of contractual liabilities of petitioners in reliance on the permits subsequent to their purchase of the property.

 

817 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Roher v. Dinkins


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


40 A.D.2d 956; 338 N.Y.S.2d 441; 1972 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3216



December 1, 1972 



DISPOSITION: Except as so modified, the judgment is affirmed, without costs and without disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, city election board and state attorney general, sought review of a judgment of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), which declared that N.Y. Educ. Law § 2590-c( 6)(34) was unconstitutional insofar as it purported to permit vacancies to be filled for the entire unexpired term of a previously elected community board member. The judgment declared that certain offices were to be deemed vacant as of a specific date.


OVERVIEW: The trial court entered a judgment holding that N.Y. Const. art. XIII, §§ 3, 4, which limited to as short a term as possible the tenure of an appointee to a vacancy in elective office, were applicable to elected community board members in New York City. The judgment held that N.Y. Educ. Law § 2590-c( 6)(34) was unconstitutional insofar as it purported to permit vacancies to be filled for the entire unexpired term of a previously elected community board member. The judgment declared that the certain offices would be deemed vacant as of a specific date. The court affirmed the judgment, but vacated the portion of it declaring that the offices would be deemed vacant. The court held that (1) the offices would be deemed vacant only for the purpose of choosing successors to appointed officers under N.Y. Pub. Off. Law § 5; and (2) the matter of appropriate further relief was left for initiation by the legislature or the governor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that New York's education law was unconstitutional insofar as it purported to permit vacancies to be filled for the entire unexpired term of a previously elected community board member, but it vacated part of the order that declared that the certain offices would be deemed vacant as of a specific date.

Glucksman v. Department of Correctional Services


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


40 A.D.2d 927; 338 N.Y.S.2d 172; 1972 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3243

819 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Sanford v. Rockefeller


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


40 A.D.2d 82; 337 N.Y.S.2d 688; 1972 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3385; 81 L.R.R.M. 2815



November 16, 1972 



DISPOSITION: Order modified, on the law and the facts, by dismissing the petitions in the Sanford, Winkowski and Splatt proceedings, and by remitting the Godbee proceeding to Special Term for a determination as to the sufficiency of the objections filed, and, as so modified, affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state employees and respondent state officials appealed an order of the Supreme Court at Special Term in Albany County (New York), which granted the state officials' motion to dismiss the state employees' petition on behalf of all others similarly situated and denied the state officials' motion to dismiss the petition in all other respects. The state employees had filed an action against the state officials to annul a determination.


OVERVIEW: The state employees received a notice from one of the state officials that they had engaged in a strike in violation of N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 210. Thereafter, the state employees filed affidavits that contained a statement of facts to show that they had not engaged in the strike. The state employees also commenced proceedings for a judgment annulling the determination that they were in the strike and for a judgment declaring §§ 210(1), 210(2)(b), (d), (e), (f), (h) unconstitutional. The state officials responded by filing a motion to dismiss the petitions. The trial court in part granted the state officials' motion. The court modified the trial court's order and, as modified, affirmed the trial court's order. The court held that due process did not require that an employee should have been granted a hearing on his objections prior to the imposition of penalties under § 210(2)(f), (g) in all actions that involved strikes by public employees, as the procedures outlined under § 210 constituted sufficient due process. The prevention of strikes by public employees involved a "valid governmental interest" that justified the procedure for imposing penalties prior to a hearing.


OUTCOME: The court modified the trial court's order by reversing the trial court's determination that the penalty procedures set forth in a statute were unconstitutional and, as modified, affirmed the trial court's order. The court also dismissed three of the state employees' proceedings and remitted the other state employee proceeding to the trial court.


HEADNOTES

Civil service -- strike by public employees -- due process does not require that employee should be granted hearing prior to imposition of penalties (Civil Service Law, § 210, subd. 2, pars. [f], [g]) in cases involving strikes by public employees -- penalty provisions not unconstitutional and do not operate as bill of attainder -- public interest justifies procedure which permits imposition of penalties  [***2] prior to hearings -- legislation which differentiates between strikes by public employees and employees in private industry is reasonable -- motion to dismiss some petitions on ground that they fail to exhaust administrative remedies should be granted -- determination that one petitioner was not entitled to hearing is subject to review in article 78 proceeding -- Special Term properly determined that class action was not appropriate.

1. Due process does not require that an employee should be granted a hearing on his objections prior to the imposition of the penalties prescribed by the Civil Service Law ( § 210, subd 2, pars. [f], [g]) in cases involving strikes by public employees.

2. The contention that the penalty provisions of section 210 are unconstitutional and that such provisions operate as a bill of attainder is without merit. The statutory procedures constitute sufficient due process.

3. While the penalties provided by the statute, both as to loss of tenure and loss of pay, affect property rights of the employee, the public interest involved justifies the procedure which permits imposition of penalties prior to a hearing on the determination by the chief executive [***3] officer that the public employee had engaged in a strike.

4. Legislation which differentiates between strikes by public employees and employees in private industry is reasonable and does not offend against the constitutional guarantee of equal protection of the law.

5. In the proceedings involving petitioners Sanford, Winkowski and Splatt, the motions to dismiss their petition, on the ground that they have failed to exhaust their administrative remedies, should be granted. After the hearings which they have been granted, it may be determined that their objections will be sustained, which would preclude any further review by them and, therefore, these proceedings for review are premature.

6. However, in the proceeding involving petitioner Godbee, since his objection was denied and it was determined that he was not entitled to a hearing, that determination is subject to review in this article 78 proceeding. The Godbee proceeding should be remitted to Special Term for a determination as to the sufficiency of the objections filed.

7. The State employees affected by the notices issued by the Director of the Office of Employee Relations fall into three groups: (1) those who filed objections [***4] and were granted a hearing; (2) those who filed objections and were denied a hearing; and (3) those who failed to file objections. Special Term properly determined that a class action was not appropriate because different questions were involved as to each employee and determination of the merits of each objection would turn on the particular facts and circumstances involved.

 

820 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Holden v. Alexander


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


39 A.D.2d 476; 336 N.Y.S.2d 649; 1972 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3663



October 24, 1972 



DISPOSITION: Order reversed, with $ 10 costs and disbursements, and motion denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff administrator filed an action against defendant owner, seeking damages for the wrongful death and pain and suffering of the administrator's intestate. The Supreme Court at Special Term (New York) entered an order granting the owner's motion to dismiss the wrongful death cause of action. In response, the administrator appealed.


OVERVIEW: The administrator's intestate was born out of wedlock. Her mother died about 11 years later. According to the administrator, he and his wife reared his intestate from the time that she was seven days old until she was placed in a foster home just before her death. The intestate died as the result of injuries suffered in a car accident. The car was operated by the owner's intestate. The administrator claimed that he was the father, and he was entitled to pursue damages for his intestate's wrongful death, even though he had not obtained an order of filiation declaring him to be the father. The owner, in support of her motion to dismiss the wrongful death cause, contended that there were no distributees surviving the administrator's intestate and, therefore, pursuant to N.Y. Est. Powers & Trusts Law § 5-4.1, an action for wrongful death could not be maintained. On appeal, the court held the administrator established his paternity of the intestate by open and complete acknowledgment. The court then found that denial of the motion to dismiss was warranted because the administrator was entitled to treatment as a distributee for the purpose of maintaining the cause of action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that granted the owner's motion to dismiss, and denied the motion to dismiss, with $ 10 costs and disbursements.


HEADNOTES

Children born out of wedlock -- right of putative father to maintain wrongful death action -- putative father is found entitled to be treated as distributee of illegitimate child for purpose of maintaining action for her wrongful death, even though no order of filiation was ever entered -- as applied to specific facts of case, statutory provision requiring entry of order of filiation before illegitimate child or father may inherit from other is declared unconstitutional.

1. The putative father of an illegitimate child who died in an automobile accident at the age of 17, without a will and without any known surviving distributees, is found entitled to be treated as a distributee for the purpose of maintaining an action for her wrongful death, even though no order of filiation was ever entered, where he has competently established his paternity, by open and complete acknowledgment.

2. As applied to the [***2] specific facts of this case, involving the right to maintain a wrongful death action, EPTL 4-1.2 (subd. [a], par. [2]; subd. [b]), requiring, inter alia, that an order of filiation be entered before an illegitimate child or his father may inherit from the other, is declared unconstitutional.

 

821 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Avant


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


39 A.D.2d 389; 334 N.Y.S.2d 768; 1972 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3959



July 19, 1972 



DISPOSITION: Order reversed, on the law, and indictments reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of an order of the County Court of Albany County (New York) that granted defendants' motion to dismiss indictments accusing defendants of offering a false instrument for filing in the first degree, violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 175.35, and grand larceny in the second degree, violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 175.35.


OVERVIEW: The charges arose out of an investigation into snow removal contracts between defendants and a city. As part of the investigation, defendants signed a waiver of immunity, under N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 103-b, and testified before the grand jury. In their motion to dismiss, defendants argued that § 103-b, which required contractors to waive immunity in investigations involving public contracts or lose the right to bid on future contracts for five years, was unconstitutional because it denied them their Fifth Amendment right against self-incrimination. The court rejected the argument, and reversed the dismissal of the indictments. In so ruling, the court held that § 103-b merely placed a special duty on contractors who applied for public contracts due to the trust placed in them in relation to public funds. The court explained that defendants consented to the provisions of § 103-b, and encumbered their Fifth Amendment privilege, at a time when the choice was unfettered. Consequently, the court found that defendants had not been coerced into testifying. Moreover, the court found that § 103-b was a valid exercise of police power, which did not unduly impinge upon a contractor's rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the supreme court's order granting defendants' motion to dismiss the indictments, and reinstated the indictments.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- offering false instrument for filing -- grand larceny -- in course of investigation of snow removal contracts and procedures between defendants and City of Albany, defendants signed waivers of immunity prior to testifying and producing books and records (cf. General Municipal Law, § 103-b) -- their testimony was properly used as basis for indictments which charged offering false instrument for filing and grand larceny -- indictments, based on testimony following execution of waivers, did not violate any constitutionally protected right.

In the course of an investigation of snow removal contracts and procedures between defendants and the City of Albany, testimony and the production of certain books and records were obtained from them pursuant to subpoena. Prior to testifying and producing the books and records, they [***2] signed waivers of immunity limiting their testimony to contracts and transactions with any political subdivision mentioned in section 103-b of the General Municipal Law which, in part, provides: "Any person who, when called before a grand jury * * * to testify in an investigation concerning any transaction or contract had with the state, any political subdivision thereof * * * refuses to sign a waiver of immunity against subsequent criminal prosecution or to answer any relevant question concerning such transaction or contract, and any firm, partnership or corporation of which he is a member, partner, director or officer shall be disqualified from thereafter selling to or submitting bids to or receiving awards from or entering into any contracts with any municipal corporation * * * for goods, work, or services, for a period of five years after such refusal or until disqualification shall be removed". Defendants' testimony was used as a basis for the indictments against them. The statute is a valid exercise of police power of the State for a justifiable purpose which, in balance, transcends the individual rights in question. When defendants voluntarily executed the waivers, the fact [***3] that their testimony resulted in subsequent indictment did not violate any constitutionally protected right. ( Garrity v. New Jersey, 385 U.S. 493; Gardner v. Broderick, 392 U.S. 273, distinguished.) The indictments should be reinstated.

 

822 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Kesselbrenner v. "Anonymous"


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


39 A.D.2d 410; 334 N.Y.S.2d 738; 1972 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3960



July 19, 1972 



DISPOSITION: Order reversed insofar as appealed from, on the law, without costs, and application for commitment of respondent granted to the extent of committing him to an appropriate institution in the State Department of Correction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant administrator sought review of a decision of the Supreme Court at Special Term in New York County (New York), which refused to commit appellee mental patient to a state hospital for the criminally insane pursuant to N.Y. Mental Hyg. Law § 85 after finding that the mental patient was dangerously mentally ill.


OVERVIEW: The mental patient was a civilly committed indigent patient in a state hospital. After several violent outbursts resulting in injuries to others, the administrator of the state hospital initiated proceedings, pursuant to § 85, to have the mental patient declared dangerously mentally ill and transferred to a state hospital for the criminally insane run by the department of corrections. The trial court found the mental patient dangerously mentally ill but refused to transfer the mental patient on the grounds that commitment in the hospital for the criminally insane would violate the mental patient's right to due process and equal protection. On appeal by the administrator, the court reversed the trial court's refusal to commit the mental patient and found that commitment of the mental patient was constitutional because has was afforded due process as to the determination that he was dangerously mentally ill and as to the right to receive periodic review of his status. The classification of mentally ill persons as either insane or dangerously insane was a reasonable distinction for the purposes of determining the type of custodial or medical care to be given.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that portion of the trial court's order that denied the administrator's application to have the mental patient committed to a state hospital for the criminally insane run by the department of corrections and ordered the application granted.


HEADNOTES

Insane and other incompetent persons -- transfer to Matteawan State Hospital -- error, upon finding that person in Manhattan State Hospital was dangerously ill within meaning of Mental Hygiene Law ( § 85), to deny application by director of said hospital that person be committed to Matteawan State Hospital -- statutory provision for transfer to Matteawan ( Mental Hygiene Law, § 85, subd. 1) does not deny equal protection of law or due process -- Supreme Court of United States in Baxstrom v. Herold (383 U.S. 107) has approved procedure prescribed by statute -- no significance in omission  [***2] of word "treatment" in Correction Law ( § 400, subd. 1) -- care includes and imports "treatment" -- differences in regulations in hospitals under jurisdiction of Departments of Correction and Mental Hygiene do not constitute denial of equal protection.

1. Section 85 of the Mental Hygiene Law provides for the mandatory transfer of a civilly committed patient in a State hospital to Matteawan State Hospital following a determination that he is dangerously mentally ill. Petitioner, director of Manhattan State Hospital, made an application pursuant to the Mental Hygiene Law ( § 85, subd. 1) for an examination of respondent, an involuntary civil mentally ill patient at Manhattan State Hospital, by two examining physicians, alleging that respondent was dangerously mentally ill. The two examing physicians certified that he was "so dangerously mentally ill that (his) presence in a hospital in the Department of Mental Hygiene is dangerous to the safety of other patients therein, the officers or employees thereof, or to the community." A hearing was held and respondent was represented by counsel at the hearing. Special Term found that respondent was dangerously mentally ill within the [***3] meaning of the statute but denied the petitioner's application. This was error and the application for commitment of the respondent should be granted.

2. The requirement of the Mental Hygiene Law ( § 85, subd. 4) that, upon a finding that a patient is dangerously mentally ill, "the judge shall forthwith issue his order hospitalizing him in the Matteawan state hospital for a period not to exceed six months from the date of such order" does not deny respondent the constitutional right of either equal protection of the laws or due process of law.

3. The Supreme Court of the United States in Baxstrom v. Herold (383 U.S. 107) tacitly approved the procedure prescribed by section 85 of the Mental Hygiene Law and recognized that commitment thereunder to Matteawan State Hospital is constitutional where an indigent person, entitled to civil status, is dangerously mentally ill and is afforded procedural due process as to the determination that he is dangerously mentally ill and the right to periodic review of his status.

4. Respondent was afforded all of the procedural due process required for commitment under section 85 of the Mental Hygiene Law. Undoubtedly, respondent would have [***4] been entitled to a jury trial of the issues presented but he did not request a jury trial.

5. There is no significance in the omission of the word "treatment" in the mandate to the Department of Correction ( Correction Law, § 400, subd. 1) to maintain hospitals for the mentally ill "solely for the purpose of holding in custody and caring for such mentally ill persons". The word "care" includes and imports the "treatment" of such persons. Moreover, Matteawan State Hospital is adequately staffed to provide the necessary treatment and care commensurate with the needs of civil patients transferred there pursuant to section 85 of the Mental Hygiene Law.

6. While there are differences in the internal operation of hospitals under the jurisdiction of the Departments of Correction and Mental Hygiene, the more restrictive regulations governing the former are proper and warranted by the need to protect ordinary civil mental patients from others in the same class who are dangerously mentally ill. The difference in regulations does not constitute a denial of equal protection of the laws.

7. There is no merit in the argument that the proportion of patients in State hospitals who are poor and [***5] disadvantaged is higher than in other types of mental hospitals, that transfers under section 85 necessarily fall with greater impact on the poor, and that this constitutes a denial of equal protection of the laws.

 

823 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Felder


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


39 A.D.2d 373; 334 N.Y.S.2d 992; 1972 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3968



July 13, 1972 



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the County Court, Nassau County, rendered March 12, 1971 on resentence, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the Nassau County Court (New York) that convicted defendant of robbery in the first degree and grand larceny in the third degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that N.Y. Penal Law § 160.15(4) was unconstitutional because it created a presumption of guilt and thus would compel him to be a witness against himself. In affirming, the court held that defendant's argument failed because placing the burden of proof on defendant as to a fact peculiarly within his knowledge did not deny him the benefit of the presumption of innocence. The court found that the state still had to establish every element of the substantive crime and defendant was offered the opportunity to assert an affirmative defense, but was not forced to do so. Therefore, defendant was not compelled to a witness against himself.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the trial court that convicted defendant of robbery in the first degree and grand larceny in the third degree.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- robbery with gun -- self incrimination -- when People prove that defendant displayed gun and thus committed robbery in first degree, defendant is not unconstitutionally compelled to testify that gun was unloaded or inoperable and so he only committed robbery in second degree (Penal Law, § 160.15, subd. 4; § 160.10, subd. 2, par. [b]); rather, defendant can offer no evidence, or evidence of others that he is innocent or that no gun was used or that gun was unloaded or inoperable; nor need his defenses be consistent with each other; statute is constitutional -- trial court should not have permitted People's witness, detective, to remain in courtroom while other witnesses testified; however, defendant was not prejudiced thereby -- trial court should not have spoken on telephone with prospective defense witness without knowledge of defense counsel;  [***2] however, in context, this error was not sufficient for reversal.

1. The Penal Law provides (§ 160.10): "A person is guilty of robbery in the second degree when he forcibly steals property and when * * * 2. In the course of the commission of the crime or of immediate flight therefrom, he or another participant in the crime * * * (b) Displays what appears to be a pistol, revolver or other firearm." However, on the same proof, he is guilty of robbery in the first degree (Penal Law, § 160.15, subd. 4); "except that in any prosecution under this subdivision [4], it is an affirmative defense that such pistol, revolver or other firearm was not a loaded weapon * * * capable of producing * * * serious physical injury". When the defendant raises such affirmative defense "at a trial," he "has the burden of establishing such defense by a preponderance of the evidence" (Penal Law, § 25.00, subd. 2). Here, the People's case established that the defendant displayed a gun and thus robbed the complainant. The People could not actually produce the gun. Thereupon the defendant took the stand and denied any robbery and any gun. The jury properly found him guilty, as charged, of robbery [***3] in the first degree.

2. Subdivision 4 of section 160.15 of the Penal Law does not unconstitutionally compel a defendant who is charged with first degree robbery to incriminate himself of second degree robbery. After the People have proved that the defendant committed a robbery with a gun, the defendant can choose whether or not to offer any evidence. If he chooses, he can testify or he can offer the evidence of others that he is innocent, or that the gun was unloaded or inoperable, or that he has other defenses. Nor need his defenses be consistent with each other. The situation does not compel him to incriminate himself.

3. Witnesses should be excluded from the courtroom while other witnesses are testifying, particularly where the testimony is in any measure corroborative or cumulative. Thus, it is regrettable that the trial court permitted one of the People's witnesses, a detective, to remain in the courtroom to assist the prosecution throughout the trial. However, it is not shown that defendant was prejudiced thereby.

4. During a recess, the trial court spoke on the telephone with a prospective defense witness about his possible testimony, without the knowledge of defense [***4] counsel. This was injudicious, but, in the context of this jury trial, it was not reversible error.

Nattin Realty, Inc. v. Ludewig


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


40 A.D.2d 535; 334 N.Y.S.2d 483; 1972 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3971
