People v. Black


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


34 A.D.2d 999; 312 N.Y.S.2d 849; 1970 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 4432



June 22, 1970 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by People v. Black, 30 N.Y.2d 593, 281 N.E.2d 849, 1972 N.Y. LEXIS 1457, 330 N.Y.S.2d 804 (1972)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.

 

890 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Penn Cent. Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


34 A.D.2d 278; 311 N.Y.S.2d 150; 1970 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 4614



June 2, 1970 



DISPOSITION: Judgment and order affirmed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant railroad commuter carrier sought review of an order of the Supreme Court at Special Term, Albany County (New York), which granted a motion by respondent State of New York for summary judgment, and from the judgment entered thereon. The Public Service Commission (PSC) initiated the action pursuant to N.Y. Pub. Serv. Law § 56 to recover a penalty for noncompliance with so much of its order as demanded a response.


OVERVIEW: The carrier asserted that only those orders of the PSC, which were within the competence of the commission and properly served, were entitled to complete compliance and further contended that where a failure of compliance was a result of a reasonable doubt in the mind of the utility's counsel as to the legality of the order or the service obviating the necessity of compliance, then no penalty could follow. In the court's view, it was improper for the carrier to fail to comply with the statute in view of the choice given it to reject the order and refuse obedience so long as done in writing in the prescribed time. The requirement that the carrier respond to the order within 10 days was not unreasonable and did not deprive it of its right to petition for rehearing. N.Y. Pub. Serv. Law § 23 sought an affirmative or negative reply but did not rule out an intermediate response. However, it demanded a response and particularized the manner in which that response was to be made. The record was clear that the carrier refused to comply with a valid and effective order of the PSC and consequently was in violation of N.Y. Pub. Serv. Law § 56, rendering itself liable to forfeiture.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and order.


HEADNOTES

Public utilities -- power of Public Service Commission -- Public Service Commission had authority (Public Service Law, § 23) to direct defendant to notify commission in writing whether its order was accepted and would be obeyed -- letters sent by attorney for defendant stating that order exceeded authority of commission were insufficient -- defendant, having refused to comply with valid and effective order of commission, was in violation of section 56 of Public Service Law and liable to forfeiture.

The Public Service Commission, having found that service of defendant railroad was deficient and needed improvement, executed an order directing "That Penn Central Company shall within ten days of the date of service of this order notify the Commission in writing whether this order, all of its terms and conditions and the revised standards of service [***2] are accepted and will be obeyed." Counsel for the railroad wrote to the Public Service Commission stating that the order "exceeds the authority of the Commission" and "I have advised the appropriate officers of my client not to accept service on this basis". Section 23 of the Public Service Law provides: "Within a time specified in the order of the commission every person and corporation upon whom it is served must if so required in the order notify the commission in writing, whether the terms of the order are accepted and will be obeyed and in the case of a corporation such notification shall be signed and acknowledged by a person or officer duly authorized by the corporation to execute such acceptance and agreement." In this action by the Public Service Commission pursuant to section 56 of the Public Service Law to recover a penalty for noncompliance with so much of its order as demanded a response, Special Term properly granted judgment to the Public Service Commission. It was improper for the railroad to fail to comply with the statute in view of the choice given it to reject the order and refuse obedience so long as done in writing in the prescribed time. The requirement that [***3] it respond within 10 days was not unreasonable and did not deprive it of its right to petition for a rehearing. The Public Service Law ( § 23, subd. 1) does not allow the Public Service Commission to require a utility to answer affirmatively. Instead, it permits the Public Service Commission to determine whether a utility is satisfied with a directive issued to it. Moreover, the statute does not rule out an intermediate response. Letters sent by the attorney for defendant were insufficient to satisfy the requirements of the order since they merely set forth attorney's legal advice. The railroad refused to comply with a valid and effective order of the Public Service Commission and consequently was in violation of section 56 of the Public Service Law, rendering itself liable to forfeiture as therein provided.

 

891 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Di Giangiemo


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


34 A.D.2d 960; 312 N.Y.S.2d 381; 1970 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 4648



June 1, 1970 



DISPOSITION: Judgment upon indictments Nos. 21771-21771A affirmed. No opinion. Judgment of resentence upon indictment No. 18158 reversed, on the law, and case remitted to the County Court for a hearing to determine the constitutionality of the 1954 conviction, and for resentence in accordance with the determination made upon the hearing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the County Court, Nassau County (New York), which (1) adjudged him in violation of probation under a prior conviction, and resentenced his as a second offender; and (2) convicted him of burglary in the third degree and grand larceny in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was (1) adjudged in violation of probation under a prior conviction, and resentenced his as a second offender based on a 1954 felony conviction, and (2) convicted of burglary in the third degree and grand larceny in the first degree. On appeal, defendant contended that his 1954 conviction was unconstitutionally obtained and that his guilty plea under the prior 1964 conviction was in reliance upon a promise that he would be sentenced as a first felony offender. The court reversed the judgment-resentencing defendant upon the probation violation and remitted for a hearing and resentence. The court held that the sentencing court erred in resentencing defendant upon the probation violation, because it failed to hold a hearing regarding defendant's constitutional challenge to the validity of the 1954 conviction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment-resentencing defendant upon the probation violation, as a second offender, and remitted for a hearing and resentence.

 

892 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Nicolette v. Clyde


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


34 A.D.2d 202; 310 N.Y.S.2d 896; 1970 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 4743



May 21, 1970 



DISPOSITION: Controversy unanimously determined in favor of plaintiffs, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners and defendant village sought a declaration as to the correct method of applying a veteran's exemption under N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law § 458 and of computing the tax due so far as the landowners and others similarly situated were concerned.


OVERVIEW: The landowners and the village submitted a controversy to the court, seeking a declaration as to the correct method of applying a veteran's exemption under N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law § 458 and of computing the tax due so far as the landowners and others similarly situated were concerned. The village contended that in many tax districts property was assessed at only a percentage of true value and that the use of different percentages in arriving at assessed value caused veterans living in different taxing districts to be treated unequally, caused nonexempt property to bear a disproportionate share of the tax burden, and constituted an unlawful delegation of legislative powers. The court held that the village had no standing to attack the validity of § 458 and that, because the landowners made no claim for repayment of taxes paid, the court did not reach the question of whether they were entitled to a refund. The village was required by § 458 to deduct the landowner's exemptions, not from the full or equalized value of their property, but from the assessed value of property.


OUTCOME: The court determined the controversy unanimously in favor of the landowners, without costs, and directed that judgment be granted without costs in favor of the landowners declaring that the village was to deduct veterans' exemptions from the assessed value of property and not from the full or equalized value.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- exemption -- veteran's exemption -- veteran's real property exemption under Real Property Tax Law ( § 458) must be deducted from assessed value and not from full or equalized value.

1. Plaintiffs, owners of a house and lot, are eligible for a veteran's real property tax exemption under Real Property Tax Law ( § 458) in the amount of $ 5,000. Prior to 1969 a 40% equalization rate was applied to the full value of the property to arrive at an assessed value of $ 5,480. The veteran's exemption of $ 5,000 was subtracted from the assessed value leaving a taxable balance of $ 480. In 1969 the veteran's exemption of $ 5,000 was subtracted from the full value of $ 13,700 leaving a "net full value" of $ 8,700. A 40% equalization rate was applied to this figure to arrive at a "taxable assessed value" of $ 3,480. Subdivision 1 of section 458 of the Real Property Tax Law provides for a veteran's exemption not to exceed $ 5,000 and sets forth the manner in which the exemption is to be applied. Section 458 of the Real Property Tax Law states that all property shall [***2] be assessed in the same manner and that the veteran's exemption must be deducted from assessed value. The method used prior to 1969 complies with these provisions. That used in 1969 does not. In the future the village should deduct veterans' exemptions from the assessed value of property and not from the full or equalized value.

2. The question whether this interpretation renders the statute unconstitutional is not reached since the defendant has no standing to attack the validity of the statute.

894 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


In re M.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


34 A.D.2d 761; 310 N.Y.S.2d 399; 1970 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 4892



May 12, 1970 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Order of the Family Court entered September 4, 1969 adjudging appellant to be a juvenile delinquent reversed, on the law, without costs and without disbursements, and the petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile sought relief from a decision by the Family Court (New York) that found that the juvenile committed acts that if done by an adult would have constituted the crimes of burglary and arson and adjudged him delinquent. The juvenile asserted that the family court erred in entering judgment against him without allowing him the safeguards during trial provided under N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 399.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile sought relief from the family court's delinquency adjudication. The court reversed. It found that the sole evidence connecting the juvenile with the acts of alleged arson and burglary consisted of the testimony by an accomplice to those acts. However, during his hearing on a charge of juvenile delinquency, the juvenile was denied the safeguards that the accomplice testimony be supported by independent proof linking the accused to the crime. Thus, he was deprived of fair treatment and equal protection of the law. The testimony of an accomplice did not become more reliable because the accused was a juvenile rather than an adult. In fact, the necessity for supporting evidence was even more essential in view of the nature of the juvenile proceedings. A hearing conducted on a charge of juvenile delinquency had to fully comply with the due process requirements. Also, a finding of guilt in a delinquency case had to rest upon proof beyond a reasonable doubt. The assertion that the evidence against the juvenile still sufficiently established the acts charged by a preponderance of the evidence was invalid. The court reversed the trial court's decision.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order issued by the family court finding the juvenile to be delinquent.

896 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Rogoff v. Anderson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


34 A.D.2d 154; 310 N.Y.S.2d 174; 1970 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 4951; 74 L.R.R.M. 2442



May 5, 1970 



DISPOSITION: Order and judgment (one paper) entered on April 22, 1969, unanimously reversed on the law, without costs and without disbursements, and summary judgment granted in favor of defendants declaring the statute and rule attacked to be constitutional; and the Clerk is directed to enter judgment accordingly.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of an order from the Supreme Court at Special Term in New York County (New York), which granted summary judgment in favor of respondent labor union, and declared that N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 207(3)(b), which required respondent to make a certain affirmation, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The labor union had commenced an action to declare unconstitutional N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 207(3)(b), which required the labor union to make a certain affirmation before the city could certify the labor organization. The trial court had granted summary judgment in favor of the labor union, and declared that § 207(3)(b) was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's judgment, and directed that summary judgment be entered in favor of the city. Section 207(b)(3) required that the labor union make an affirmation that it did not assert the right to strike against any government, to assist or participate in any such strike, or to impose an obligation to conduct, assist or participate in such a strike. The court found such a requirement was constitutional, and it did not infringe upon the labor union's first amendment rights. The court held that such a requirement where collective bargaining certification was involved was neither burdensome nor unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order that granted summary judgment in favor of the labor union. The court directed that summary judgment be entered in favor of the city, and declared that the statute under attack was constitutional.


HEADNOTES

Civil service -- certification of public employee organization -- statute (Civil Service Law, § 207) and rule (Consolidated Rules of the Office of Collective Bargaining of City of New York, rule 2.17, subd. b) which make filing of affirmation that employee organization does not assert right to strike against government, to assist or participate in any strike, or to impose obligation to conduct, assist or participate in such strike, as condition precedent to certification of such employee organization as exclusive bargaining representative, not constitutionally defective -- statute and rule not construed as infringing on rights protected by First Amendment.

 Section 207 of the Civil Service Law provides: "For purposes of resolving disputes concerning [***2] representation status * * * the board * * * shall

3. certify or recognize an employee organization upon * * * (b) the affirmation by such organization that it does not assert the right to strike against any government, to assist or participate in any such strike, or to impose an obligation to conduct, assist or participate in such a strike." Rule 2.17, subd. b of the Consolidated Rules of the Office of Collective Bargaining of the City of New York, pursuant to statutory power, makes the filing of such an affirmation a condition precedent to certification of a public employee organization as exclusive bargaining representative. The requirement of the statute and the rule is not construed as infringing upon the exercise of rights protected by the First Amendment. The effect on free expression is not so evident as to warrant their rejection as unconstitutional. Certification is here involved and the requirement therefor in neither burdensome nor unreasonable. The statute and rule are not constitutionally defective.

 

897 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


8200 Realty Corp. v. Lindsay


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


34 A.D.2d 79; 309 N.Y.S.2d 443; 1970 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 5142



April 9, 1970 



DISPOSITION: Order and judgment (one paper) entered on October 2, 1969, unanimously reversed and vacated, on the law, with $ 50 costs and disbursements to the appellants; plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment granted; and judgment directed to be entered declaring and decreeing that the New York City Rent Stabilization Law of 1969 (Administrative Code, tit. YY, ch. 51) is unconstitutional and invalid and declaring the same void and annulled in its entirety. The judgment to be so entered shall, however, be in all respects stayed pending the further order of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant realtors sought review of the judgment of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), which granted a motion by respondents, mayor and other individuals, for summary judgment and dismissed the complaint. The realtors challenged the constitutionality and validity of the Rent Stabilization Law of 1969 (New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code § YY51 (1969)).


OVERVIEW: The realtors brought an action under the rent stabilization law and sought to have it declared unconstitutional. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which had dismissed the complaint, and held that the law failed to represent a proper and valid exercise of the legislative authority reposed in the city. The court found that by the provisions of the law, the city associated itself with the functions of a private landlord's association, which was supported by private funds, and thus was a private corporation and could not be considered as a city instrumentality. The court also found that the association was given the power to collect dues from its members and used the moneys received in furtherance of the purposes of the law, which amounted to the taxing of a particular class of landlords for the purpose of administering and enforcing the city rent control regulations, and constituted an invalid delegation of the legislative taxing powers of the city. The court held that the law violated equal protection because those landlords who became and remained members of the association were a favored class.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and held that the newly enacted rent and conviction control law was unconstitutional and invalid and declared it void and annulled in its entirety.


HEADNOTES

Landlord and tenant -- rent regulation -- Rent Stabilization Law of 1969 of City of New York providing for rent control over post-1947 apartments is unconstitutional.

The Rent Stabilization Law of 1969 (Local Laws, 1969, No. 16 of City of New York; Administrative Code of City of New York, tit. YY, ch. 51) enacted for the [***2] purpose of extending rent control to apartment houses completed after February, 1947 is unconstitutional in that the city delegates to a landlords' association, a private association, power which the city itself has, to administer rent control, in that the city delegates legislative power to the private association in the form of rule-making, which rules are binding on landlords, in that the law in effect gives the association power to tax a particular class of landlords for administering rent control, and in that it denies equal protection of the laws by favoring landlords who become members of the association and tenants whose landlords are not members of the association. There is no reasonable basis for this preferred treatment.

 

898 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Fitzpatrick


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


34 A.D.2d 730; 311 N.Y.S.2d 577; 1970 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 5156



April 9, 1970 



DISPOSITION: Application unanimously denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought a writ of prohibition to prevent the Oneida County Court (New York) from exceeding its authorized powers in an action (defendant's trial on four counts of murder) in which it allegedly lacked jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with four counts of murder including counts of capital murder. He moved to waive a jury trial on the grounds that the indictment did not allege that the victim was a police officer. The county court denied the motion on a showing by the state that it would show that defendant shot two police officers who were performing their duties. Defendant also filed a motion to dismiss the indictment on the grounds that the murder statutes were unconstitutional. The county court denied that motion as well. Defendant then sought an action in prohibition to prevent the county court from exceeding its authorized powers in an action over which it had no jurisdiction. Defendant raised the same issues as he raised in his motions to waive jury trial and to dismiss. The court denied the writ of prohibition. The court held that the questions petitioner raised could be adequately reviewed on appeal. Prohibition was an extraordinary remedy which was not used when the grievance could be redressed by ordinary proceedings or merely to prevent error which could be easily corrected on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's application for writ of prohibition to prevent the county court from adjudicating his murder trial.

 

899 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Buffalo v. J. W. Clement Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


34 A.D.2d 24; 311 N.Y.S.2d 98; 1970 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 5135



April 9, 1970 



DISPOSITION: Judgment modified on the law and facts in accordance with the opinion by Witmer, J., and as modified affirmed, with costs to J. W. Clement Company.

Order entered January 22, 1969 modified in accordance with the opinion by Witmer, J., and as modified affirmed.

Second order entered January 22, 1969 modified in accordance with the opinion by Witmer, J., and as modified affirmed, and matter of extra allowance and statutory costs remitted to trial court for determination in accordance with the opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city appealed a judgment of the Supreme Court at Trial Term in Erie County (New York) awarding over $ 2 million in a condemnation proceeding filed by the city to acquire title to real property owned by defendant property owner. The property owner cross-appealed orders denying its application to modify the judgment and to assess fees, costs, and disbursements.


OVERVIEW: The city commenced a condemnation proceeding to acquire title to waterfront property owned by the property owner for purposes of an urban renewal plan. The city advised the property owner in 1957 that the taking would occur between 1960 and 1962. In 1961, the property owner bought another site and began building and moving his business in anticipation of the taking. At the condemnation trial, the trial court found that a de facto taking of the property occurred as of 1963, from which time the city should have assumed the cost of maintaining the property, which it did not. The trial court found that the acts of the city, including its protracted delay, destroyed the value of the property and that the city, by its threat of condemnation, forced the property owner to move its business operation. The court affirmed the trial court's findings, holding that there was a de facto taking by the city as of 1963, even where there was no physical invasion or direct legal restraint, because the city so interfered with the use of the subject property that essential elements of ownership were destroyed. The court also affirmed the trial court's valuations of the land and building.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the property owner as well as the trial court's valuation of the land and building. The court modified the award as to the issue of moving expenses. The court held that the trial court erred in denying the property owner statutory costs and disbursements and in denying an extra allowance for costs.


HEADNOTES

Eminent domain -- de facto condemnation -- city's acts, from first indicating its intent to condemn defendant landowner's property in 1954 until actual taking in January, 1967, resulted in de facto taking of defendant's premises as of date  [***2] defendant removed from premises in April, 1963 -- court properly valued land at $ 175,000 and building at $ 525,000 -- award of $ 84,000 for taxes, etc. since de facto taking is affirmed -- defendant owner is entitled to costs of moving printing machinery in amount proved by owner and not lesser amount -- notice of removal of fixtures to city was not required -- filing of separate notice of claim for removal of fixtures was not required -- award for fixtures not removed was improper -- interest at 4% and for later periods at 6% is allowed -- Buffalo City Charter (§ 393) does not authorize extra allowance -- for charter provisions governing condemnation to be constitutional, provision of Condemnation Law is read into it; so read, defendant is granted extra allowance -- trial court erred in denying statutory costs -- owner's application for payment of its counsel fees was properly denied.

1. Commencing in 1954, plaintiff city made known to defendant landowner that it planned to take the landowner's property for an urban renewal project. Commencing in 1960, various officials advised defendant that it must get out within anywhere from 1 1/2 to 4 years. In 1962, the Mayor advised [***3] defendant that it would negotiate for price of the property in the spring of 1963. Defendant bought a site for relocation in 1961 and moved out of the subject property in April, 1963. Formal condemnation did not occur until January, 1967. There was a de facto taking by the city's conduct which deprived defendant of the beneficial use of its property. The city's acts forced defendant to move from its property in April, 1963 rendering the property unsalable and unrentable. There was such taking even absent a physical invasion or legal restraint because the city so interfered with the use of the subject property that essential elements of ownership were destroyed and substantial justice cannot otherwise be had.

2. The landowner's expert computed value by estimating net rental income, deducting land value, and capitalizing the result. He obtained a building value of $ 656,236 and land value of $ 193,766. In view of the lower values presented by the city, the court properly found land value of $ 175,000 and building value of $ 525,000.

3. An additional award to defendant for $ 84,000 in reimbursement for its expenses for taxes, insurance and maintenance of the premises since [***4] the de facto taking in April, 1963 is supported by the record and is affirmed.

4. Printing machinery in the building was an integral part of a going business on the premises which constituted fixtures for which compensation must be awarded. Since the machinery was movable, and the cost of moving it ($ 869,819.20) was far less than its value in place ($ 4,478,000) less the resale or salvage value ($ 509,250), plaintiff must pay only the moving costs. Since the city offered no contrary evidence of such costs, the award of $ 785,000 was error and defendant owner is entitled to $ 869,819.20 for its moving costs.

5. The owner gave the city adequate notice of its intention to remove the fixtures, but, in any event under the circumstances of this case, no notice was required.

6. Just compensation to the owner requires that the city pay for the reasonable cost of removing the fixtures and, therefore, the filing of a separate notice of claim was unnecessary.

7. The award to the owner of $ 84,000 for installed fixtures is reversed since it is reasonable to assume that these items were not removable without substantially damaging the freehold and cannot be the subject of a separate [***5] award.

8. Interest at 4% per annum is allowed from April 1, 1963 to August 1, 1966 (State Finance Law, § 16, as amd. by L. 1966, ch. 921, eff. August 1, 1966) and thereafter at the rate of 6% until entry of the judgment and 6% should accrue upon the judgment. The Legislature in adopting the 6% interest rate in 1966 indicated a rate of interest which is fair and just considering the rights and interests both of claimants and the public. Moreover, defendant landowner failed to produce evidence to show that it is entitled to a higher interest rate.

9. Section 393 of the Buffalo City Charter governing the procedure in condemnation proceedings cannot be read to authorize an extra allowance of costs.

10. Article 21 of the Buffalo City Charter, governing condemnation proceedings commenced by the city insofar as it denies a landowner an extra allowance for costs, deprives the landowner of equal treatment under the law since another condemnor in the city must pay an extra allowance under the Condemnation Law. To be sustained as constitutional, subdivision 2 of section 16 of the Condemnation Law must be incorporated into article 21. An extra allowance is granted.

11. The trial court [***6] erred in denying defendant statutory costs and disbursements.

12. The owner's application for payment of its counsel fees was properly denied.

 

900 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


In re D.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


34 A.D.2d 41; 310 N.Y.S.2d 82; 1970 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 5136



April 9, 1970 



DISPOSITION: Motion to dismiss appeal denied. Order reversed on the law and facts and matter remitted to Onondaga County Family Court for further proceedings not inconsistent with the opinion by Gabrielli, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile challenged an order of the Family Court (New York), adjudging him to be a juvenile delinquent based on an act which, if committed by an adult, would constitute a felony.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile was charged with being a juvenile delinquent in having intentionally shot and killed his father. The juvenile's requests for a jury trial were denied as was his motion for an order to require the county attorney to prove its case beyond a reasonable doubt. The juvenile subsequently admitted to a lesser charge and was adjudged to be a juvenile delinquent. The court reversed and remitted the case. The court declared that N.Y. Fam. Ct. Act § 744(b), insofar as it required proof by a mere preponderance of the evidence, was unconstitutional and held that it was error to deny the juvenile's motion for a direction regarding the burden of proof. Although the juvenile admitted to a lesser charge, the court held that his admission was not voluntary because it was the result of the deprivation of his constitutional rights. The court held that the juvenile was entitled to a jury trial because he was charged with juvenile delinquency involving a serious crime and faced the possibility of incarceration of more than one year.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and remitted the case for further proceedings to determine whether the juvenile was a juvenile delinquent based on an act which, if committed by an adult, would constitute a felony.


HEADNOTES

Infants -- right to jury trial -- jury trial required in Family Court proceeding charging person with being juvenile delinquent based on act which, if committed by adult, would constitute felony -- infant's admission of acts contained in substituted petition was extracted in impermissible manner and was not voluntarily made -- Family Court Act ( § 744, subd. [b]), insofar as it requires proof by mere preponderance of evidence, is unconstitutional -- requirement of jury trial limited to charges involving serious crimes.

1. The Sixth and Fourteenth Amendments to the United States Constitution require a jury trial in a Family Court proceeding charging a person with being a juvenile delinquent based on an act which, if committed by an adult, would constitute a felony.

2. After the denial of the infant's several motions [***2] for a jury trial, the Assistant County Attorney stated that, if the infant would admit the allegations of a new petition, charging him with an act which, if performed by an adult, would be a violation of section 120.25 of the Penal Law -- reckless endangerment in the first degree -- he would move for a dismissal of the old petition which had charged acts which, if done by an adult, would constitute the crime of murder. The infant admitted the charge and was subsequently adjudged a juvenile delinquent. The infant did not waive or bargain away his constitutional rights by admitting the charge in the second petition. His admission of the acts contained in the substituted petition was extracted in an impermissible manner. In the light of all the circumstances, the admission was not voluntarily made. He has been denied the essentials of due process and was deprived of constitutional rights.

3. Section 744 (subd. [b]) of the Family Court Act, insofar as it requires proof by the mere preponderance of the evidence, is unconstitutional.

4. The declaration that a jury trial should be afforded to a youth charged with being a juvenile delinquent based on an act which, if committed by [***3] an adult, would constitute a crime is limited to those charges involving serious crimes as defined in Duncan v. Louisiana (391 U.S. 145) and Matter of Hogan v. Rosenberg (24 N Y 2d 207).

 

901 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Nixon


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


33 A.D.2d 403; 309 N.Y.S.2d 236; 1970 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 5270



March 25, 1970 



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the County Court of Tompkins County (New York), which convicted him on his plea of guilty of the crime of reckless endangerment in the second degree under N.Y. Penal Law § 120.20.


OVERVIEW: The police investigated a disturbance at the home of defendant's mother-in-law. Defendant, who was pounding on the door of the home, pointed a gun at the officer. Defendant dropped the gun only after the officer hit defendant over the head. Defendant pled guilty to reckless endangerment in the second degree. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. The trial court did not err in denying defendant's demurrer to the indictment of reckless endangerment in the first degree. The requirements of N.Y. Code Crim. Proc. §§ 275, 276 were met because the indictment designated the crime charged, set forth the date and place of the crime, and described the criminal act. N.Y. Penal Law § 120.20, to which defendant pled guilty, was not unconstitutionally vague. The trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence as untimely because it was made on the eve of trial. The trial court's denial of defendant's motion to inspect the grand jury minutes was proper and was not appealable. Defendant's motion to dismiss the indictment as insufficient was properly denied where it was supported only by defendant's allegations upon information and belief and conclusion of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for reckless endangerment in the second degree upon his guilty plea.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- reckless endangerment -- indictment upon which defendant was convicted on his plea of guilty of reckless endangerment in second degree ( Penal Law, § 120.20) conforms to requirements of Code of Criminal Procedure (§§ 275, 276) -- statute not unconstitutionally vague and indefinite -- trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence made on eve of trial, 12 months after indictment -- in any event, arrest without warrant was lawful -- denial of motion to inspect Grand Jury minutes was proper and, in any event, not appealable -- sentence imposed not excessive.

1. Defendant was convicted on his plea of guilty to the crime of reckless endangerment in the second degree ( Penal Law, § 120.20). The indictment designates the crime charged, sets forth the date and place, where and when the act constituting the crime occurred and describes the criminal act, and accordingly, conforms to the requirements [***2] of sections 275 and 276 of the Code of Criminal Procedure.

2. Section 120.20 of the Penal Law which defines reckless endangerment in the second degree is not unconstitutionally vague and indefinite.

3. The trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence as untimely, since such motion was made on the eve of trial, some 12 months after the indictment. There was no justification for defendant's delay in making his motion to suppress.

4. In any event defendant's arrest without a warrant was lawful, as the police officers had probable cause to make the arrest, and the search and seizure were valid as incident thereto.

5. The trial court's denial of defendant's motion to inspect the Grand Jury minutes was proper, particularly in view of the fact that the trial court found that the testimony before the Grand Jury was in main the same testimony as presented at the preliminary examination.

6. In addition, a denial of a motion to inspect the Grand Jury minutes is not appealable.

7. Defendant's motion to dismiss the indictment as insufficient was supported only by defendant's affidavit containing allegations upon information and belief and conclusions of law. A presumption [***3] of regularity attaches to the Grand Jury proceedings and the indictment, and the presumption cannot be overcome by an affidavit such as defendant's.

8. The sentence imposed was not excessive. The court here considered the seriousness of defendant's act, his underlying problem of alcoholism, and the probation report submitted to it prior to sentence. It cannot be said that the trial court abused its discretion in imposing the sentence it did.

People ex rel. Pilgrim v. Quick


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


34 A.D.2d 562; 310 N.Y.S.2d 1011; 1970 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 5327



March 13, 1970 

 

903 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Tinsley v. Monserrat


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


33 A.D.2d 316; 307 N.Y.S.2d 888; 1970 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 5418



February 26, 1970 



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed on the law, without costs and without disbursements, the stay of the election vacated, and the petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Board of Education of the City of New York sought review of a judgment from the Supreme Court at Special Term in New York County (New York), which annulled a school district plan for the Borough of Manhattan under N.Y. Educ. Law § 2590-b and stayed an election.


OVERVIEW: After the Board approved the plan, petitioner presidents of parents associations sued the Board, claiming that the plan violated the statute's requirement to retain racially, culturally, and ethnically integrated school districts. When the supreme court annulled the plan and stayed an election, the Board sought review. The court reversed the judgment, vacated the stay, and dismissed the petition. Neither the plan nor the statute was repugnant to the constitution. The final plan was arrived at by constraint of the statute's inflexible mandate in respect of the minimum pupil population of a district. The Board fully complied with statute. The policy against both de facto and de jure segregation was not violated. The tentative plan mapped and delineated the boundaries of six proposed districts. Only two districts had more than the prescribed 20,000 minimum. The Board exercised its discretion within its statutory powers. How it was to be done was the Board's concern, not the court's. The opponents of the final plan sought a new opportunity to attack it. A new hearing would have accomplished no more than to permit them to state again their support of the abandoned tentative plan.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment, which annulled the plan and stayed the election, vacated the stay of the election, and dismissed the parents associations' petition.


HEADNOTES

Schools -- plan for creation of school districts -- New York City Board of Education in accordance with Education Law ( § 2590-b) caused publication of proposed plan for creation of school districts in Manhattan; plan proposed six districts all but two of which contained less than 20,000 pupils; criteria listed in statute for school district included requirement that each district contain not less than 20,000 pupils; proposed plan noted that it was not possible to meet that criterion with six districts but that board had sought assurances from Legislature to permit board to retain six districts; hearing  [***2] was held and thereafter board adopted plan containing five districts, all containing more than 20,000 pupils; no deception on part of board; no new hearing required; plan is constitutional -- statute is constitutional -- board complied with statute; stay of election is vacated.

1. Section 2590-b of the Education Law requires the members of the interim Board of Education of the City of New York to adopt a plan for the creation of school districts. The statute provides that such school districts contain not less than 20,000 pupils. The board proposed a plan for the Borough of Manhattan containing six districts all but two of which contained less than 20,000 pupils. The plan set forth the criteria mentioned in the statute, and then noted that it was not possible to retain six districts while adhering to the mandate of a minimum of 20,000 pupils, but that the board had sought assurances that the Legislature would permit the board to retain the six districts. A hearing was held and thereafter the final plan was promulgated with five districts, each district containing a minimum of 20,000 pupils. There was no deception on the part of the board in proposing the tentative plan. It [***3] noted that the six district plan could not meet the 20,000 pupil requirement. No new or further hearing is required. While no legally permissible plan was submitted prior to the hearing the entire subject was submitted for discussion at the hearing. The final plan was arrived at by constraint of the statute's inflexible mandate in respect of the minimum pupil population of a district. The plan does not deny equal protection of the law. There is in the plan neither de facto nor de jure segregation.

2. The statute is not unconstitutional. It sets up reasonable and proper procedures and standards.

3. The board complied with the statute. The judgment is reversed, the petition dismissed and the stay of election is vacated.

Contino v. Hempstead


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]

905 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Posner v. Rockefeller


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


33 A.D.2d 314; 307 N.Y.S.2d 957; 1970 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 5449



February 24, 1970 



DISPOSITION: Order and judgment affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state legislators challenged an order and judgment of the Supreme Court at Special Term, Albany County (New York), that granted a motion by respondents, governor and legislature, to dismiss the legislators' petition for a judgment declaring that certain portions of appropriation bills enacted by the legislature violated N.Y. Const. art. VII and prohibiting respondents from expending further moneys.


OVERVIEW: The legislators originally filed their petition in another county, where respondents moved for a change of venue and to dismiss the petition. That trial court denied respondents' motions and granted judgment to the legislators, but an intermediate appellate court vacated the judgment and the order denying the motion for change of venue and remanded the case to the trial court whose venue respondents had sought in their motion. After that decision was affirmed by the court of appeals, the legislators commenced their proceeding anew with an order to show cause. The trial court dismissed the proceeding, holding that they lacked standing and that the proceeding was time-barred. The court affirmed the order and judgment. The trial court did not err in entertaining respondents' motion to dismiss. The motion filed in the other county's trial court was transferred to the trial court when the case was transferred and was properly before the trial court. The mere status of citizen-taxpayer did not confer standing upon the legislators, and their status as legislators did not give them standing to challenge the appropriations in the absence of a deprivation of due process or equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that granted respondents' motion to dismiss the legislators' petition and the judgment entered on the order.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- State budget -- petition in proceeding brought by three New York State Assemblymen, who contended that appropriation bills enacted by New York State Legislature violate article VII of New York State Constitution, properly dismissed -- status as citizen-taxpayer or as Assemblyman not sufficient to permit challenge of constitutionality of State Legislature acts or acts of State officers -- motion to dismiss proceeding properly before court.

1. The petition in a proceeding brought by three New York State Assemblymen, who contended that certain portions of the appropriation bills submitted by the Governor of New York and enacted into law by the New York State Legislature in 1969, violate article VII of the New York State Constitution, was properly dismissed. The mere status of a citizen-taxpayer is not sufficient to confer standing to [***2] challenge the constitutionality of the acts of the State Legislature or of State officers. To bring such a proceeding the taxpayer must show, in addition, that he is personally aggrieved and there is no such allegation by the petitioners here.

2. The fact that petitioners are Assemblymen does not give them standing to bring the instant proceeding. For a public body or official to challenge a State statute, it must be shown that there has been some deprivation of due process or equal protection of the law. They have not been denied due process, or equal protection and, therefore, lack standing as Assemblymen to bring this proceeding.

3. The proceeding was originally commenced in Supreme Court, New York County. The respondents moved for a change of venue to Albany County and also to dismiss the petition on several grounds. Special Term denied respondents' motion and granted judgment to the petitioners on the merits. On appeal the Appellate Division, First Department, vacated the order and judgment of the Supreme Court and remanded the proceedings to Special Term, Albany County. This decision was affirmed by the Court of Appeals. The petitioners, thereafter, commenced this proceeding [***3] anew. It was not error to entertain a motion to dismiss. Such a motion was before the court in the original proceeding, which was transferred to Albany County. Consequently, all of the papers were necessarily transferred to the Albany County Clerk's office and were properly before the court.

 

906 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Eastman Kodak Co. v. State Tax Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


33 A.D.2d 298; 307 N.Y.S.2d 69; 1970 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 5632



January 29, 1970 



DISPOSITION: Determination confirmed, with costs to respondent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayer sought review of a decision from respondent State Tax Commission (commission), which denied the taxpayer's application for revision or refund of franchise tax assessments.


OVERVIEW: A taxpayer had an arrangement with an independent contractor to sell the taxpayer's product which was manufactured in the state and was to be sold on consignment nationally. Taxes were assessed and the taxpayer objected. When the commission denied the taxpayer's petition for revision or refund of franchise tax assessments the taxpayer sought review. The court determined that sales made outside the state were properly included in the numerator of the New York state formula because the order for those sales were deemed accepted in New York and the procedure used to make the assessment was not unconstitutional. The court confirmed the commission's determination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the commission's decision assessing taxes.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- franchise tax -- by contract with taxpayer, foreign corporation acquired exclusive right to sell film manufactured by taxpayer in New York State -- foreign corporation remitted net sales price less commisisons to taxpayer -- sales by such foreign corporation of taxpayer's goods located outside New York at time of sale were properly deemed attributable to this State pursuant to Tax Law ( § 210, subd. 3, par. [a], subpar. [2], cl. [D]) -- inclusion of such orders not unconstitutional -- if taxpayer is paying franchise tax in excess of 100% on part of its income because three other States levy franchise tax, New York's formula is not unreasonable.

1. The franchise tax statute, with regard to sales of tangible personal property [***2] attributable to New York, provides: "An order shall be deemed received or accepted within the state if it has been received or accepted by an employee, agent, agency or independent contractor chiefly situated at, connected with by contract or otherwise, or sent out from a permanent or continuous place of business of the taxpayer within the state." (Tax Law, § 210, subd. 3, par. [a], subpar. [2], cl. [D]). In substance the formula states that sales of tangible personal property not located in New York at the time the order is made or received will be attributable to New York when the property is not located at the time of the receipt of the order at a permanent place of business maintained by the taxpayer outside the State and where the orders are received or accepted within the State. During the years in question a foreign corporation and the taxpayer entered into contracts whereby the foreign corporation acquired the exclusive right to sell and distribute unexposed professional motion picture film manufactured by the taxpayer in New York State. Upon making a sale and withdrawing film from the inventory, the foreign corporation was obligated to remit the net sales price less [***3] its commissions to the taxpayer. The taxpayer had no control over the manner and method in which the foreign corporation performed its business of obtaining and consummating sales. The foreign corporation's connection with the taxpayer by the contracts and their performance was almost exclusively with the taxpayer's Rochester office. These sales of the petitioner's goods located outside the State of New York at the time of sale were properly deemed attributable to this State pursuant to the Tax Law.

2. The inclusion of the orders received for petitioner's products outside of the State of New York in the tax formula under consideration herein is not unconstitutional. Net income from the interstate operations of a foreign corporation may be subjected to State taxation provided the levy is not discriminatory and is properly apportioned to local activities within the taxing State. The Due Process Clause will not be contravened if the taxes imposed are levied only on that portion of the taxpayer's net income which arises from its activities within the taxing State.

3. One who attacks a formula of apportionment carries a distinct burden of showing by clear and cogent evidence that [***4] it results in extraterritorial values being taxed. That burden has not been met in this case.

4. The Tax Commission states, in effect, that all of taxpayer's sales activities are in New York. "Sales activity" does not mean literal selling activity, but any corporate activity relating to sales. New York State is not attempting to reach the sales activity of the petitioner outside of this State.

5. However, taxpayer is paying a franchise tax in excess of 100% on a part of its income. In addition to New York, California, New Jersey and Illinois are levying a franchise tax on taxpayer for its activity in those States. Logically it is impossible, when the tax is fairly apportioned, to have the same income taxed twice. In practical operation, however, the possibility of the contrary is not foreclosed. In the present case it cannot be said that it is New York's formula that is unreasonable in application.

 

907 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Sawyer


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


33 A.D.2d 242; 306 N.Y.S.2d 494; 1970 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 5725



January 15, 1970 



DISPOSITION: Judgment unanimously reversed on the law and action remitted to Oneida County Court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the County Court of Oneida County (New York), which rendered a judgment convicting defendant of being a youthful offender after he consented to being tried without a jury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with robbery, second degree, and attempted robbery, second degree, in violation of N.Y. Penal Law §§ 160.10 and 110.00. The grand jury did not recommend youthful offender treatment, although defendant's age would have made him eligible pursuant to N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law §§ 913-e and 913-g. Upon arraignment, defendant and his attorney executed written consent providing that if found eligible for adjudication as a youthful offender, he consented to be tried without a jury, should a trial be had. Defendant was found eligible for adjudication as a youthful offender, pled guilty and was sentenced pursuant to N.Y. Penal Law § 75, which permitted imprisonment for up to four years. He appealed the sentence. The court reversed, holding that the trial court was deprived of jurisdiction to impose such a sentence because the crime was a serious one as defined by case law and the constitutional right of a youthful offender to a trial by jury applied thereto. Defendant was effectively denied that right when he was required to consent to a nonjury trial as a prerequisite to consideration for adjudication as a youthful offender.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court convicting defendant of being a youthful offender.


HEADNOTES

Infants -- youthful offenders -- statutes (Code Crim. Pro., § 913-g, subd. 3; § 913-h), insofar as they require one between ages of 16 and 19 to consent to summary trial, without jury, to render him eligible for youthful offender treatment, are unconstitutional -- conviction of being youthful offender reversed and matter remitted.

The statutes (Code Crim. Pro., § 913-g, subd. 3 and § 913-h), insofar as they require one between the ages of 16 and 19 to consent to a summary trial without a jury to render one eligible for youthful offender treatment, are unconstitutional. Appellant herein who consented, pursuant to the statutory requirement, to be tried without a jury as a condition to being investigated for youthful offender treatment was sentenced to Elmira Reformatory pursuant to the provisions of article 75 of the Penal Law. The trial court was without jurisdiction to impose such a sentence ( [***2] Matter of Hogan v. Rosenberg, 24 N Y 2d 207). The conviction of defendant of being a youthful offender is reversed and matter remitted.

 

908 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Oates v. Oates


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


33 A.D.2d 133; 306 N.Y.S.2d 108; 1969 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2552



December 16, 1969 



DISPOSITION: The order of this court entered on December 16, 1969, is vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant creditor sought review of an order of the Supreme Court at Special Term (New York), which vacated a subpoena duces tecum served upon the respondent, mother of the debtor, in regard to a judgment obtained against the debtor for unpaid alimony and support of the debtor's children.


OVERVIEW: A judgment was obtained against the debtor for unpaid alimony and support of the debtor's children. Thereafter, the debtor fled the jurisdiction. The creditor then served a subpoena duces tecum on the debtor's mother. The mother filed a motion to vacate such subpoena in regard to the validity of the service of the subpoena and the right to examine. The supreme court granted the motion, and the creditor appealed. On review, the court reversed the order of the supreme court. The court found that service had been attempted pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 308(3). The court stated that in the light of the prima facie showing, the failures to deny except by argument and attorney's conclusory statements, while the persons with knowledge maintained a discrete silence, indicated clearly that the motion to vacate on the ground of invalid service was a pure sham. As per the right to examine, the court held that the judgment creditor's assertion that the witness knew the present whereabouts of the debtor was certainly relevant to obtaining satisfaction of the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order of the supreme court, which order vacated the creditor's service of a subpoena duces tecum upon the mother.


HEADNOTES

Judgments -- supplementary proceedings -- motion to vacate subpoena in supplementary proceedings served on mother of judgment debtor, who had fled jurisdiction, should be denied -- service was valid -- validity of service as ground for motion to vacate is sham -- "matter relevant to the satisfaction of the judgment" ( CPLR 5223) satisfactorily shown.

1. A motion to vacate a subpoena in supplementary proceedings served on the mother of the judgment debtor who had fled the jurisdiction should be denied. The service was valid. Because the process server made several unsuccessful attempts to serve the witness, service was made pursuant to CPLR 308 (subd. 3) by leaving the subpoena with a man at the building listed as the witness' home with the telephone company. The validity [***2] of service as a ground for the motion to vacate is sham.

2. All that need be shown under CPLR 5223 to secure examination of the third party is "matter relevant to the satisfaction of the judgment." The judgment creditor asserts that the witness knows the present whereabouts of the debtor, which would be relevant to obtaining satisfaction of the judgment. Also it is alleged that the witness has a joint bank account with the debtor.

Mobile Home Owners Protective Assoc. v. Chatham


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


33 A.D.2d 78; 305 N.Y.S.2d 334; 1969 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 4841



November 25, 1969 



DISPOSITION: Order and judgment affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mobile home owners appealed from a decision of the Columbia County Supreme Court at Special Term (New York), which granted defendant town's motion for summary judgment and dismissed the owners' complaint seeking a declaration that a town ordinance regulating mobile homes was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to N.Y. Town Law § 130(21), which authorized the town to regulate "house trailers," the town enacted an ordinance that prohibited the permanent location of mobiles homes within its boundaries except in mobile home parks. The owners, who had mounted their mobile homes upon permanent foundations on their property, sought a declaration that the ordinance was unconstitutional or that it exceeded the power of the town to regulate trailer houses under § 130(21). The trial court granted the town's motion for summary judgment and dismissed the owner's complaint. On appeal, the court held that the trial court properly dismissed the complaint because: (1) "mobile homes" were considered "trailer houses" within the meaning of § 130(21); (2) once mobile, a structure remained a "trailer" regardless of the manner in which it was affixed to a foundation; and (3) the constitutionality of discrimination against such homes as single-family residences had been previously upheld by the New York courts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.


HEADNOTES

Municipal corporations -- regulation of mobile homes -- towns are authorized to regulate "house trailers" (Town Law, § 130, subd. 21); town's ordinance restricting mobile homes to mobile home parks is constitutional -- mobile home erected on permanent foundation is "house trailer" within statute.

1. Subdivision 21 of section 130 of the Town Law authorizes a town to regulate "house trailers" and their location when used as sleeping quarters outside an established house trailer camp. Defendant town enacted an ordinance which prohibits the permanent location of mobile homes within its boundaries except in mobile home parks. Such ordinance is constitutional.

2. Individual appellants erected upon a permanent foundation upon their property a mobile home 12 feet wide by 60 feet long. The words "mobile home" as applied to appellants' structure are not different from "house trailers" within the statute.

 

910 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Ochs v. La Vallee


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


33 A.D.2d 80; 307 N.Y.S.2d 982; 1969 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2777



November 25, 1969 



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Supreme Court at Special Term, Clinton County (New York), which dismissed his application for a writ of habeas corpus without a hearing.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of larceny and rape and received concurrent indeterminate sentences of 5 to 10 years in State prison. He was paroled and remained at liberty until arrested on a federal charge. Pursuant to a parole detainer warrant, appellant was returned to prison upon the dismissal of the federal charge. At a parole revocation hearing, he demanded the assistance of retained counsel, but permission was denied, and he was remanded to prison. Thereafter he petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus on the ground that refusal to permit representation was a deprivation of his constitutional rights. The trial court granted the application to the extent of ordering a new hearing with such representation. All of the requests of counsel were denied, and appellant was remanded to prison. He again petitioned for habeas corpus relief alleging that the rehearing was inadequate to allow effective counsel. The trial court dismissed the petition. Appellant argued that N.Y. Correct. Law § 218 was unconstitutional. The court held that the only right granted to appellant under § 218 was to offer an explanation as to the charge that he has violated his parole.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Parole -- revocation hearing -- at parole revocation hearing, only right of parolee is to offer explanation of charge that he violated parole; he has no constitutional right to representation by counsel, to confrontation of witnesses and to production of proof.

Upon a parole revocation hearing accorded the parolee under section 218 of the Correction Law, the only right granted to the parolee is to offer an explanation as to the charge that he violated parole. Parolees do not have any constitutional right to representation by counsel, to confrontation of witnesses or to production of proof at such hearing. Since a parolee is at all times subject to the judgment of conviction, it is not reasonable or necessary that he be accorded any right beyond the right to appear before the Parole Board and offer his explanation.

 

911 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Gorniakowski v. Ingraham


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


33 A.D.2d 32; 304 N.Y.S.2d 841; 1969 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2888



November 6, 1969 



DISPOSITION: Determination annulled, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner pig farmer brought a proceeding under N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 to review a determination of respondent Commissioner of Health of the State of New York that required the farmer to abate the emission of odors into the atmosphere emanating from the operation of his pig farm. The Commissioner found that the farmer violated N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 10, § 186.1. The proceeding was transferred to the court by a supreme court.


OVERVIEW: The farmer argued that the Air Pollution Control Act, N.Y. Pub. Health Law art. 12-A and the regulations implementing it were inapplicable to agriculture and also unconstitutionally vague. On appeal, the court held that (1) the court did not need to resolve the important and complex issues raised by the farmer because N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 10, § 186.1 failed as applied to comply with N.Y. Pub. Health Law §§ 1271(2)(a), 1276(4) in that the regulation gave no recognition to variations in geographic areas; (2) since no standards for the farmer's area had been issued at the time of the order appealed from, there existed no valid basis to determine that the farmer's activity was polluting the air; and (3) although standards were later promulgated for the farmer's area, he clearly was not accountable for violation of a statute where its meaning could not be determined without implementing regulations not yet in existence.


OUTCOME: The court annulled the Commissioner's determination.


HEADNOTES

Health -- air pollution -- order of Commissioner of Health directing pig farmer in Schenectady County to cease emitting odors into air is vacated since regulation of Air Pollution Control Board claimed to have been violated is invalid as not in compliance with Public Health Law.

An order of the Commissioner of Health requiring petitioner to abate the emission of odors into the atmosphere emanating from the operation of his pig farm in Schenectady County must be vacated in that the regulation promulgated by the Air Pollution Control Board and found to have been violated by petitioner (10 NYCRR 186.1) failed to comply with paragraph (a) of subdivision 2 of section 1271 and subdivision 4 of section 1276 of the Public Health Law because the board failed to "prepare [***2] and develop a general comprehensive plan for the control or abatement of existing air pollution * * * recognizing varying requirements for different areas of the state". The regulation allegedly violated fails to give any recognition to variations in geographic areas, and is thus invalid. Since no standards for Schenectady County had been issued at the time of the instant order, there existed no valid basis to determine that petitioner's activity was "polluting" the air.
